GT Equivalence Verification (BPG14)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*(c4 - exp(-c5*P))*P + c6*P*exp(-c7*t)
Candidate formulas: 56

Let  
\[
\text{GT}(t,P)=a\Big[(1-\tfrac{P}{b})P+(1-e^{-kP})P+P e^{-kt}\Big]
\]
with fixed \(a=0.11423898258902421\), \(b=40.69810220267985\), \(k=0.08368363514073095\).

So GT has these structural “signatures”:

1) **A quadratic polynomial part in \(P\)**:  
\[
a\,(P-\tfrac{1}{b}P^2)
\]
2) **A mixed term \(P(1-e^{-kP})\)** which equals \(aP - aP e^{-kP}\): it contains **\(P e^{-kP}\)** with a **negative exponent in \(P\)**.
3) **A time-decay term \(aP e^{-kt}\)**: exponential in \(t\) with **negative** rate, multiplied by \(P\).
4) GT is smooth in \(P\) (no \(|P|\)), and has **no standalone constants** (value is 0 at \(P=0\) for all \(t\)).

Now check candidates: almost all share a template
\[
P\cdot(\text{something in }t) \;+\; P\cdot(\text{something in }P)\;+\;(\text{extra terms in }|P|,\;P^2,\;constants,\;logs,\;sins,\;etc.)
\]
To match GT, we must be able to produce simultaneously:
- \(+aP\) and \(-\frac{a}{b}P^2\) (polynomial),
- \(-aP e^{-kP}\) (negative exponent in \(P\)),
- \(+aP e^{-kt}\) (negative exponent in \(t\)),
- and **avoid** any \(|P|\), \(\log\), \(\sin\), rational-in-\(t\), etc., unless they can be zeroed out.

### Key obstruction across the list
All candidates that include \(P*c2*exp(P*c3)\) can only generate \(P e^{(+c3)P}\), i.e. an exponential with **linear exponent in \(P\)**. We could set \(c3=-k\) to get \(P e^{-kP}\), good.  
But GT needs **both** a polynomial term \((P - \frac{1}{b}P^2)\) **and** the \(P(1-e^{-kP})\) term, which includes an additional **\(+aP\)** besides \(-aP e^{-kP}\). That extra \(+aP\) must come from some other term (like \(P*c4\) or similar). Then we still need the \(-\frac{a}{b}P^2\) term, which would require an explicit \(P^2\) term (not \(|P|^2\) unless we accept mismatch for negative \(P\)), and we must also match the \(t\)-exponential with negative rate.

Also, every candidate’s \(t\)-exponential term is \(P*c0*exp(c1*t)\), which can match \(aP e^{-kt}\) by setting \(c0=a\), \(c1=-k\). That part is fine.

The real issue is: **none of the candidates provide a clean way to produce exactly the polynomial \(aP-\frac{a}{b}P^2\) while also producing \(aP-aP e^{-kP}\), without introducing forbidden \(|P|\) behavior or extra constants, and while keeping equality for all real \(P\).**

Below is the candidate-by-candidate reasoning (grouping repeated obstructions).

---

## Candidates 1–3
1. \(P c0 e^{c1 t} + P c2 e^{Pc3} + P c4 (c5+t)^{c6} + c7|P|^2 + c8|P|\)

- Can match \(P e^{-kt}\) via \(c0=a, c1=-k\).
- Can match \(P e^{-kP}\) via \(c2=-a, c3=-k\).
- But GT also needs polynomial \(aP-\frac{a}{b}P^2\). Candidate has no \(P\) or \(P^2\) polynomial term except via \(|P|^2\) and \(|P|\), and a \(t\)-power term \(P(c5+t)^{c6}\) which cannot equal a constant-in-\(t\) linear/quadratic polynomial in \(P\) for all \(t\) unless set to 0 (set \(c4=0\)).  
- \(|P|^2\neq P^2\) for negative \(P\) (it equals \(P^2\) actually, but \(|P|^2 = P^2\) always; however \(|P|\) is non-smooth and cannot appear in GT). We can set \(c8=0\). Then \(c7|P|^2\) could supply a \(P^2\) term. But we still need a **linear \(+aP\)** term and a **quadratic \(-\frac{a}{b}P^2\)** term simultaneously. There is no pure \(P\) term available (only exponentials and the killed power term). So cannot.
→ **No match**.

2. Similar, but has rational-in-\(t\) terms and \(|P|\). Those must be zeroed; still no pure \(P\) term.
→ **No match**.

3. Same as (1) plus constant \(c7\). GT has no constant offset (must be 0), so would require \(c7=0\). Still lacks pure \(P\) term.
→ **No match**.

## Candidate 4
\(P c0 e^{c1 t} + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c4|P|^2 + c5|P| + c6|P|/(c7+|P|)\)

- Can set \(c5=c6=0\) to remove \(|P|\) and rational term.
- Then we have \(P c0 e^{c1 t} + P c2 e^{Pc3} + c4 P^2\).
- Still missing the needed **linear polynomial term \(+aP\)** and also the **\(+aP\)** coming from \(P(1-e^{-kP})\) if we set \(P c2 e^{Pc3}\) to \(-aP e^{-kP}\). There is no separate \(+aP\) term.
→ **No match**.

## Candidates 5–9
These add \(P^{c4}c5\), log, \(t\)-dependent terms, etc., plus \(|P|\) terms.

- Any \(t\)-only additive term (like \(c4 e^{c5 t}\) or \(c4 t^{c5}\)) cannot appear in GT (GT is proportional to \(P\)), so must be set to 0.
- After zeroing extras, they still do not provide both a pure \(P\) term and a \(P^2\) term with correct coefficients while also having \(P e^{-kP}\).
- \(P^{c4}c5\) could be made \(c5 P^2\) by setting \(c4=2\), but then we still need a pure \(+aP\) term; not available unless another term supplies it (it doesn’t).
→ **No match** for 5–9.

## Candidate 10
\(P^2 c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + P c3 e^{Pc4} + P c5 + c6 + c7|P|^2 + c8|P|\)

- This is closer: it has \(P^2\) and \(P\) terms.
- We can set \(c6=0, c8=0, c7=0\) to avoid constant and \(|P|\).
- Set \(P c1 e^{c2 t}\) to \(aP e^{-kt}\): \(c1=a, c2=-k\).
- Set \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\) to \(-aP e^{-kP}\): \(c3=-a, c4=-k\).
- Then we still need the remaining polynomial part from GT:
  \[
  aP - \frac{a}{b}P^2 + aP \quad(\text{because } aP(1-e^{-kP})=aP-aP e^{-kP})
  \]
  Total polynomial-in-\(P\) contribution in GT is \(aP\) (from first bracket) plus \(aP\) (from second bracket) = \(2aP\), and quadratic is \(-\frac{a}{b}P^2\).
- Candidate has only one explicit \(P c5\) linear term and \(P^2 c0\) quadratic term. Great: set \(c5=2a\), \(c0=-a/b\).
- But wait: we already used \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\) to match \(-aP e^{-kP}\). Good.
- Now check: candidate’s exponential-in-\(P\) term is \(P c3 e^{Pc4}\) with no accompanying \(+aP\) inside that same term; we supplied the needed \(+aP\) via \(P c5\). That seems consistent.
- However, GT also has **another** exponential-in-\(P\) structure: it is \(aP(1-e^{-kP})\) which we decomposed as \(aP - aP e^{-kP}\). We matched \(-aP e^{-kP}\) and provided \(+aP\) via \(P c5\). So far so good.
- The remaining polynomial term \(aP - (a/b)P^2\) from the first bracket is also covered by \(P c5\) and \(P^2 c0\), but note we already set \(c5=2a\) to cover **both** linear \(aP\) terms (from first and second brackets). That works because GT’s total linear coefficient is indeed \(2a\).
- So structurally candidate 10 **can** match GT *if we ignore the \(|P|^2\) term (set \(c7=0\))*.

But candidate 10 still contains \(c7|P|^2\). Setting \(c7=0\) removes it, fine. Then candidate 10 exactly matches GT with:
- \(c1=a,\; c2=-k\)
- \(c3=-a,\; c4=-k\)
- \(c5=2a\)
- \(c0=-a/b\)
- \(c6=0,\; c7=0,\; c8=0\)

This yields:
\[
-a/b\,P^2 + aP e^{-kt} - aP e^{-kP} + 2aP
\]
which equals GT expanded:
\[
aP - a/b\,P^2 + aP - aP e^{-kP} + aP e^{-kt}
\]
Yes.

→ **Match found for candidate 10.**

## Candidate 11
Has \(P*c4 + c5\) etc. But lacks \(P^2\) unless using \(|P|^2\) (not present here). So cannot produce \(-\frac{a}{b}P^2\).
→ **No match**.

## Candidates 12–56 (excluding 52 which is similar to 10)
- 12–9x variants generally lack either:
  - a true \(P^2\) polynomial term, or
  - a pure \(P\) term, or
  - they introduce non-removable \(t\)-only terms / constants / \(|P|\) kinks / logs/sins that cannot equal GT for all \(t,P\).
- Candidate 52 is like 10 but without the standalone constant \(c6\); it still has \(P^2 c0\) and \(P c5\), so it can also match with the same parameter choices (and set \(|P|\) terms to 0).

### Candidate 52
\(P^2 c0 + P c1 e^{c2 t} + P c3 e^{Pc4} + P c5 + c6|P|^2 + c7|P|\)

Set \(c6=c7=0\) and same assignments:
- \(c1=a,\; c2=-k\)
- \(c3=-a,\; c4=-k\)
- \(c5=2a\)
- \(c0=-a/b\)

→ **Also matches.**

All other candidates either cannot form both needed polynomial degrees and the negative \(P\)-exponential simultaneously, or they force extra functional dependence (log/sin/rational) that cannot be identically zeroed without also removing required pieces.

---

Final verdict: candidates **10** and **52** can be made exactly equal to GT by parameter choice.

[MATCH FOUND]

Conclusion: Match found
